Self-Contradictions in Denying Judgment of the Sum
Second refutation: three self-contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize three self-contradictions in the opponent's claim that the sum of past events cannot be judged.

Core Idea
The opponent's own statements already judge the sum.

The author shifts to a different tactic: showing that the opponent's very assertion that the sum cannot be judged is itself a judgment. He then points out two more contradictions: the opponent's proposition about infinite past states necessarily refers to the totality, and their statement about continuity applies to the sum, not individuals. This lesson examines these three contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the second aspect passage
Read the Arabic passage beginning with 'والوجه الثاني:' and its translation.
2
Identify the three self-contradictions
The author lists three ways the opponent's claim is self-contradictory: (1) judging that no judgment is possible, (2) the subject of the proposition about infinity must be the totality, (3) the description of continuity applies to the totality.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Think about how each contradiction undermines the opponent's position. The opponent cannot avoid making judgments about the sum, so their initial claim is untenable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السؤال الثاني: وهو قوله: (مجموع الحوادث لا وجود له البتة، وما لا وجود له، يمتنع الحكم عليه بقبول الزيادة والنقصان..) فنقول: لنا في الجواب عنه وجوه: الأول: إن قولنا: مجموع الحوادث قد وجد، أعم من قولنا: مجموع الحوادث قد وجد بصفة الاجتماع. والدليل عليه: أن القائل إذا قال: رأيت جملة أهل البلد، فإنه يصح أن يقال له: أرأيت جملتهم بصفة الاجتماع أو لا بصفة الاجتماع؟ وذلك يدل على أن المفهوم من رؤيتهم بجملتهم، أعم من المفهوم من رؤية جملتهم بصفة الاجتماع. فكذلك قولنا: جملة الحوادث الماضية قد وجدت، أعم من قولنا: إن جملة الحوادث الماضية قد وجدت بصفة الاجتماع. وأنتم إنما أبطلتم هذا المفهوم الخاص. وظاهر: أنه لا يلزم من كذب الخاص، كذب العام. فثبت: أنه لا يلزم من كذب قولنا: جملة الحوادث الماضية وجدت بصفة الاجتماع: كذب قولنا: جملة الحوادث قد وجدت. بل نقول: الدليل على أن جملة الحوادث قد وجدت: أنه يصدق قولنا: إن جملة الحوادث قد وجدت بصفة الافتراق والتعاقب. وقولنا: جملة الحوادث قد وجدت، جزء من قولنا: جملة الحوادث قد وجدت بصفة الافتراق. ومتى صدق المركب، فقد صدقت أجزاؤه لا محالة. فوجب أن يصدق قولنا: إن جملة الحوادث قد وجدت. فالحاصل: أنهم أقاموا الدليل على بطلان الخاص، ثم استدلوا به على بطلان العام. وذلك باطل. وأما نحن فقد أقمنا الدلالة على صدق الخاص، ثم استدللنا به على صدق العام. وذلك حق. والوجه الثاني: إن قولهم: إن جملة الحوادث الماضية لا يصح الحكم عليها البتة: كلام متناقض من وجوه: الأول: إنهم حكموا بامتناع الحكم عليها. فهذا حكم على تلك الجملة بهذا الامتناع. فيلزم من هذا الاعتبار. والثاني: إنا إذا قلنا: الأحوال الماضية لا نهاية لها. فهذه قضية. ولكل قضية موضوع ومحمول. فالموضوع في هذه القضية، إما كل واحد من تلك الأحوال الماضية، وهو ظاهر الفساد. لأن كل واحد منها لا يصدق عليه أنه أمور متناهية. وإما كل تلك الأمور وجملتها. وحينئذ يكون هذا اعتراف بأنه يمكن الحكم على ذلك الحكم وعلى تلك الجملة، بأحكام معلومة. وذلك يبطل قولهم: إنه لا يمكن الحكم عليه البتة. والثالث: إنهم يقولون: الأحوال الماضية دائمة مستمرة من الأزل إلى الأبد. فالمحكوم عليه بالاستمرار من الأزل إلى الأبد: ليس هو كل واحد من تلك الحوادث بل مجموعها. وذلك يناقض قولهم: إن ذلك المجموع لا يمكن الحكم عليه.
As for the second question: his statement: 'The sum of past events has no existence at all, and what has no existence cannot be judged as accepting increase or decrease.' We say: We have several aspects in answering it. First: Our statement 'the sum of past events has existed' is more general than our statement 'the sum of past events has existed collectively.' The proof of that is that when someone says 'I saw the whole town's people,' it is valid to say to him: 'Did you see them collectively or not collectively?' That indicates that the concept of seeing them as a whole is more general than the concept of seeing them collectively. Similarly, our statement 'the sum of past events has existed' is more general than our statement 'the sum of past events has existed collectively.' You have only refuted this specific concept. It is apparent that the falsity of the specific does not entail the falsity of the general. So it is established that the falsity of our statement 'the sum of past events existed collectively' does not entail the falsity of our statement 'the sum of past events has existed.' Rather, we say: The evidence that the sum of past events has existed is that our statement 'the sum of past events has existed in a state of separation and succession' is true. And our statement 'the sum of past events has existed' is part of our statement 'the sum of past events has existed in a state of separation.' Whenever the compound is true, its parts are necessarily true. So it is necessary that our statement 'the sum of past events has existed' is true. The conclusion: They presented evidence for the falsity of the specific, then used it to argue for the falsity of the general. That is false. As for us, we have presented evidence for the truth of the specific, then used it to argue for the truth of the general. That is correct. Second aspect: Their statement 'the sum of past events cannot be judged at all' is self-contradictory in several ways: First: They judged that judging it is impossible. That is a judgment on that sum of this impossibility. So it follows from this consideration. Second: When we say 'past states are infinite,' this is a proposition. Every proposition has a subject and a predicate. The subject in this proposition is either each individual past state—which is clearly false, because each individual state cannot be described as being infinite—or all these things and their totality. In that case, this is an acknowledgment that it is possible to make known judgments about that judgment and about that totality. That refutes their statement that it cannot be judged at all. Third: They say 'past states are continuous from eternity to everlasting.' What is being described as continuing from eternity to everlasting is not each individual event but their totality. That contradicts their statement that this totality cannot be judged.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection claiming that the sum of past events has no existence and therefore cannot be subject to judgments like increase or decrease. The author provides two main refutations. The first refutation distinguishes between the general statement 'the sum has existed' and the specific statement 'the sum has existed collectively.' Using an analogy of seeing all the townspeople—where one can ask whether they were seen collectively or not—the author shows that the opponent's argument only disproves the specific collective existence, not the general existence. Since the general does not depend on the specific, the opponent's inference is invalid. Moreover, the author argues that the general statement is true because the sum exists in a state of separation and succession, and the compound statement (existence in separation) implies the truth of its parts (simple existence). The second refutation demonstrates that the opponent's own claims are self-contradictory. First, by stating that the sum cannot be judged, they themselves make a judgment about it. Second, when discussing infinite past states, the subject of that proposition must be the totality, implying it can be judged. Third, their assertion that past states are continuous from eternity applies to the totality, not individuals, again contradicting their claim that the totality cannot be judged.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm)
المجموع (al-majmu')
الأزلي (al-azali)
الأبدي (al-abadi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the sum of past events is completely exempt from any judgment.
Correction: Even the opponent's own statements imply judgments about the sum, so it must be possible to judge it.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the self-contradictions mentioned in this passage?
A) The opponent judges that no judgment is possible
B) The proposition 'past states are infinite' must refer to the totality
C) The sum of past events has no existence
D) The description 'continuous from eternity' applies to the totality

Key Takeaway
The opponent's own statements about the sum, such as judging it impossible or describing it as infinite and continuous, presuppose that the sum can be judged.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your own beliefs do you say, 'I cannot judge that,' even as you inevitably make judgments about it? How does this lesson expose that inconsistency in your heart?
?
When you speak about Allah's attributes or the unseen, do you ever deny you are making a judgment when you are actually describing? What would it cost you to admit that you are judging, and then ensure your judgment is from revelation?
?
If the opponent's self-contradiction is so clear, why do you think you might still cling to similar contradictions in your own theology? What is the fear that prevents you from submitting to the full truth of Allah's speech?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
15 min
Why Relational Attributes Cannot Be External Realities
Author argues that relational attributes have no external existence, thus examples involving them do not refute the argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why relational attributes cannot have external existence and how this refutes objections based on such examples.

Core Idea
Relations are not entities; they would force infinite regress.

In this passage, the author tackles a key objection to the proof of temporal origination. Critics had presented examples involving relations, such as 'effect-causing' or 'attribution'. The author argues that these examples fail because relational attributes have no external reality; if they did, absurd infinite regresses would follow. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the opening sentence to understand what objection is being answered. The objection is a 'refutation by examples' (al-naqd bi al-suwar).
The examples involve relational matters.
2
Grasp the key principle
The author states that relations (idafat) cannot exist externally. Why? Because that would require infinite regress.
This is the core of the argument.
3
Follow the example of effect-causing
The author takes the attribute 'effect-causing' (al-mu'aththiriyya) and shows that if it were an additional attribute, it leads to a contradiction: either there is an intermediary (making regress) or no effect (denying causality).
This demonstrates the absurdity.
4
Apply the conclusion
Since all the objections are based on relations, they are invalid. Contrast with past events, which are real and sequential.
This defends the original proof.
5
Reflect on the author's reflection
Note the author says this argument is the fruit of forty years of reflection, indicating its depth and importance.
Consider the care taken in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السؤال الثالث : وهو النقض بالصور المذكورة فالجواب عنه : إن هذه الصورة بأسرها أمور إضافية نسبية والإضافات والنسب يمتنع أن تكون موجودة في الأعيان ، وإلا لزمت التسلسلات والتزام التسلسل محال في العقول والدليل عليه : أن المعقول من التسلسل : التزام القول بوجود أمور متتالية متلاصقة مادة إلى غير النهاية . ومعلوم : أن هذا المعنى لا يحصل إلا عند الاعتراف بوجود أشياء متلاصقة متواصلة ، لا يتخللها شيء آخر. إلا أنا نقول : القول بكون الإضافات موجودات في الأعيان يبطل ذلك. ولنذكر تقرير هذا الكلام في مثال واحد فنقول : لو كانت المؤثرية صفة زائدة على ذات المؤثر وعلى ذات الأثر ، فهل ههنا شيء يؤثر في شيء آخر ، أم لا ؟ فإن كان الأول : لا يكون بين المؤثر وبين أثره المتصل به واسطة . إلا أن هذا مع القول بكون الإضافات أموراً موجودة في الأعيان محال . لأن كون ذلك المؤثر مؤثراً في أثره : متوسط بينهما . فحيث صدق أنه ليس بينهما متوسط صدق أنه حصل بينهما متوسط وهذا محال . وإن كان الثاني : وهو أنه ليس ههنا شيء يؤثر في شيء : كان هذا نفياً للتأثير والمؤثر وذلك باطل . وكذا القول في موصوفية الذات بالصفة . فيثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو كانت الإضافات موجودة في الأعيان لزم القول بالتسلسل، وثبت : أن ذلك محال ، فوجب القطع بأن الإضافات لا وجود لها في الأعيان البتة . ولما كان جميع النقوض التي أوردتموها من باب الإضافات ، ثبت أن شيئاً منها غير موجود في الأعيان ، لا بمجموعها ولا بأحادها ، بخلاف الحوادث الماضية ، فإنه وإن لم توجد جملتها على سبيل الاجتماع ، إلا أنه وجدت جملتها على سبيل التعاقب والتوالي فظهر الفرق . فهذا غاية ما يحضرنا في تقرير هذه الحجة ، بعد الأفكار المتوالية فيها، في مدة أربعين سنة . والله ولي التوفيق
As for the third objection, which is the refutation by the mentioned examples, the answer to it: These examples entirely are relational, attributive matters. Relations and attributes cannot exist externally; otherwise, infinite regresses would be necessary, and asserting infinite regress is rationally impossible. The proof is: The rational meaning of infinite regress is the assertion of the existence of successive, contiguous things endlessly. It is known that this meaning only occurs when acknowledging the existence of contiguous, continuous things with nothing in between. However, we say: The claim that relations are existent things in external reality invalidates that. Let us present this statement in one example: If effect-causing (al-mu'aththiriyya) were an additional attribute beyond the essence of the cause and the essence of the effect, then is there something that affects something else, or not? If the first: then there is no intermediary between the cause and its effect that is contiguous to it. However, this is impossible along with the claim that relations are existent things in external reality, because the fact that that cause is effective in its effect is an intermediary between them. So when it is true that there is no intermediary between them, it becomes true that an intermediary has occurred between them, and this is impossible. If the second: that there is no thing that affects something else, then this is a denial of effect and cause, and that is false. The same applies to the attribution of the essence with the attribute. So it is established by what we have mentioned that if relations were existent in external reality, the assertion of infinite regress would be necessary, and it is established that this is impossible. Therefore it is necessarily concluded that relations have no existence in external reality at all. And since all the refutations that you have brought are of the category of relations, it is established that none of them exist in external reality, neither in their totality nor individually, unlike past events. For although their totality does not exist collectively, yet their totality exists sequentially and successively. Thus the difference becomes clear. This is the utmost that occurs to us in establishing this argument, after successive reflections upon it over a period of forty years. And God is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage answers a third objection against the proof of temporal origination, namely that examples (suwar) involving relations refute the proof. The author first states the key principle: relational attributes (idafat) cannot exist in external reality (a'yan) because if they did, an infinite regress would follow. He then proves this by an example: consider the attribute of 'causing an effect' (al-mu'aththiriyya). If this were an additional attribute beyond the cause and effect, then either there is an intermediary or not. If we say there is no intermediary between cause and effect, then the 'causing' itself would be an intermediary, creating a contradiction. If we say there is no effect at all, that denies causality, which is false. The same reasoning applies to any attribute of a thing. Therefore, relations are not real entities, so any objection based on them (like the examples) does not apply to the actual past events, which are real entities that exist sequentially. The author concludes by noting this argument is the fruit of forty years of reflection.

Key Terms
إضافات (relations)
نسب (attributes)
تسلسل (infinite regress)
مؤثرية (effect-causing)
أعيان (external realities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that relations like 'causation' or 'attribution' are real entities that exist independently in the external world.
Correction: The author demonstrates that if they were real, they would lead to an infinite regress, which is rationally impossible. Therefore, relations are mere conceptual constructs with no external existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot relational attributes exist externally?
A) Because they are purely mental constructs.
B) Because their existence would necessitate an infinite regress.
C) Because the Qur'an denies them.
D) Because they are not mentioned by earlier scholars.

Key Takeaway
Relations are not external realities; their supposed existence leads to infinite regress, so objections based on relations do not affect the proof of temporal origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author spent forty years refining this argument. What in your faith have you not given enough time to deeply understand? Are you willing to sit with difficult truths until they become settled in your heart?
?
This lesson teaches that relational attributes (like 'father', 'teacher', 'friend') are not fixed realities but mere relations. Which relationship in your life do you treat as if it defines your very essence? How might freeing yourself from that assumption change how you live?
?
If you truly believed that no relation (status, role, or connection) exists as a permanent entity, what worldly attachments would lose their grip on your heart? Identify one such attachment and decide today to see it as transient.

intermediate

Relational Attributes: Not Real, Not External
Author refutes the third objection by proving relational attributes do not exist externally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why relational attributes cannot exist externally and how their hypothetical existence would lead to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Relational attributes are not real things; calling them real leads to an endless chain.

The objection tries to compare past events with relational attributes. But the author shows a critical difference: relational attributes, if taken as real, would create an infinite regress in causality. This lesson unpacks that argument and why past events are not like them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector had cited examples (like past events) to argue that the author's reasoning would lead to absurdities. Recognize that these examples are relational in nature.
The author is addressing a third objection (naqd) that challenges his position on past events.
2
Grasp the core claim
Read carefully: the author states that all such examples are relational (idafat) and that relations cannot exist externally because that would entail infinite regress.
Infinite regress (tasalsul) is a logical impossibility in Islamic theology.
3
Follow the proof
The author provides a concrete example: effect-producing (mu'aththiriyya). Walk through the two possibilities and see how both lead to contradiction if the attribute is real.
The same reasoning applies to any attribute qualifying an essence.
4
Distinguish from past events
Note the contrast: past events exist sequentially, whereas relational attributes have no external existence at all. This saves the original argument from the objection.
The author also shares that this argument was refined over forty years.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السؤال الثالث : وهو النقض بالصور المذكورة فالجواب عنه : إن هذه الصورة بأسرها أمور إضافية نسبية والإضافات والنسب يمتنع أن تكون موجودة في الأعيان ، وإلا لزمت التسلسلات والتزام التسلسل محال في العقول والدليل عليه : أن المعقول من التسلسل : التزام القول بوجود أمور متتالية متلاصقة مادة إلى غير النهاية . ومعلوم : أن هذا المعنى لا يحصل إلا عند الاعتراف بوجود أشياء متلاصقة متواصلة ، لا يتخللها شيء آخر. إلا أنا نقول : القول بكون الإضافات موجودات في الأعيان ، يبطل ذلك. ولنذكر تقرير هذا الكلام في مثال واحد فنقول : لو كانت المؤثرية صفة زائدة على ذات المؤثر وعلى ذات الأثر ، فهل ههنا شيء يؤثر في شيء آخر ، أم لا ؟ فإن كان الأول : لا يكون بين المؤثر وبين أثره، المتصل به واسطة . إلا أن هذا مع القول بكون الإضافات أموراً موجودة [ في الأعيان ] محال . لأن كون ذلك المؤثر مؤثراً في أثره : متوسط بينهما . فحيث صدق أنه ليس بينهما متوسط [ صدق أنه حصل بينهما متوسط ] وهذا محال . وإن كان الثاني : وهو أنه ليس ههنا شيء يؤثر في شيء : كان هذا نفياً للتأثير [ والمؤثر ] وذلك باطل . وكذا القول في موصوفية الذات بالصفة . فيثبت بما ذكرنا أنه لو كانت الإضافات موجودة في الأعيان لزم القول بالتسلسل، وثبت : أن ذلك محال ، فوجب القطع بأن الإضافات لا وجود لها في الأعيان البتة . ولما كان جميع النقوض التي أوردتموها من باب الإضافات ، ثبت أن شيئاً منها غير موجود في الأعيان ، لا بمجموعها ولا بأحادها ، بخلاف الحوادث الماضية ، فإنه وإن لم توجد جملتها على سبيل الاجتماع ، إلا أنه وجدت جملتها على سبيل التعاقب [ والتوالي ] فظهر الفرق . فهذا غاية ما يحضرنا في تقرير هذه الحجة ، بعد الأفكار المتوالية فيها، في مدة أربعين سنة . والله ولي التوفيق .
As for the third question – which is the objection by the mentioned examples – the answer to it is: These examples as a whole are relational, relative matters. Relations and relative matters are impossible to exist as external entities, otherwise infinite regresses would follow, and affirming infinite regress is impossible in intellects. The proof of that is: The understood meaning of infinite regress is affirming the existence of successive, contiguous things ad infinitum. It is known that this meaning only occurs when one acknowledges the existence of contiguous, continuous things with nothing intervening between them. But we say: The statement that relations are existents in external entities invalidates that. Let us present an exposition of this statement in one example, and say: If effect-producing (al-mu'aththiriyya) were an additional attribute beyond the essence of the producer and the essence of the effect, then does something here produce an effect in something else, or not? If the first, then there is no intermediary between the producer and its effect that is connected to it. However, this, given the claim that relations are existing matters [in external entities], is impossible. Because the fact that that producer is a producer in its effect is an intermediary between them. So wherever it is true that there is no intermediary between them, [it is true that an intermediary has occurred between them], and this is impossible. If the second – that nothing here produces an effect in anything – then this would be a denial of effecting [and the effector], and that is false. The same applies to the qualification of the essence by an attribute. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that if relations were existent in external entities, affirming infinite regress would follow, and it is established that that is impossible. So it is necessary to definitively conclude that relations have no existence in external entities at all. Since all the objections you have raised are of the category of relations, it is established that none of them exist in external entities, not collectively nor individually, unlike past events. For although the entirety of past events does not exist collectively, yet the entirety of them exists in succession [and order]. So the difference appears. This is the utmost that occurs to us in presenting this proof, after successive reflections upon it over a period of forty years. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an objection (naqd). The objector had cited examples (e.g., divine attributes, past events) to argue that if the author's reasoning about past events were applied universally, it would lead to absurdities. The author responds by analyzing the nature of the examples: they are all relational attributes (idafat). He argues: (1) Relations cannot exist externally because that would entail infinite regress (tasalsul). (2) He proves this via a concrete example: if 'producing an effect' (mu'aththiriyya) were a real, externally existent attribute, then between the producer and the effect there would be an intermediary (the attribute itself), which contradicts the fact that the effect is directly produced. If we deny the intermediary, then the attribute is not real, but then effect-production itself is denied, which is absurd. (3) The same reasoning applies to any attribute qualifying an essence. (4) Since all the objector's examples are relational, they are not externally existent, unlike past events which exist sequentially. Thus the objection fails. The author adds a personal note that this argument has been refined over forty years.

Key Terms
إضافات (relational attributes)
تسلسل (infinite regress)
موجود في العين (externally existent)
مؤثرية (effect-producing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Relational attributes are real external entities, just like past events or divine attributes.
Correction: Relational attributes are not externally existent; their hypothetical existence would cause an infinite regress, proving they are mere mental considerations.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do relational attributes (idafat) not exist externally?
A) Because they are mental concepts only
B) Because if they existed, they would cause an infinite regress
C) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran
D) Because they are self-contradictory

Key Takeaway
Relational attributes are not external realities; claiming they are leads to an infinite regress, so they are merely conceptual relations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read a proof that many of the relationships you take for granted—being a cause, being a father, even your own attributes—are not real entities outside the mind. How many of your daily identities and roles do you treat as 'real things' that define you? What would change if you saw them as mere concepts that have no independent existence? Will you take a moment today to mentally strip away these relational labels and see yourself as you are before God, without them?
?
The author says he spent forty years refining this argument. When was the last time you wrestled with a truth from the Qur'an or Sunnah for even forty minutes? Are you satisfied with superficial understanding of your creed, or will you commit to digging deeper until the proofs become clear in your heart? What one theological question will you pursue until you can defend it with the same rigor as this author?
?
If relational attributes like 'being a producer of an effect' have no external reality, then your actions and their consequences are not 'things' that cling to you. This strips away the illusion that you are burdened by your past deeds as if they are physical attachments. Are you holding onto guilt or pride over past actions as if they are real entities weighing you down? Can you let go of that false reality and instead turn to God with a heart freed from conceptual baggage? What step will you take today to release that burden?
